The Second Epistle of Paul to the

2 Thessalonians

SummaryThe book of 2nd Thessalonians is a Pauline Epistle (letter from Paul). The Apostle Paul wrote it about 52-54 A.D., several months after his first letter to the church in Thessalonica. The key personalities in this book are the Apostle Paul, Silas, and Timothy. Paul wrote this letter to reemphasize the coming return of Jesus Christ. Some of the people in Thessalonica had thought that Jesus had already returned, this letter was written to correct any misunderstandings.

•    In chapter 1, Paul highlights the great hope of Jesus’ future return although the exact time is unable to be known by anyone. He commends the church in Thessalonica for their perseverance in the midst of persecution, “we ourselves speak proudly of you among the churches of God for your perseverance and faith in the midst of all your persecutions and afflictions which you endure” (1:4). Paul teaches that God will punish those who are persecuting on the last day. “Dealing out retribution to those who do not know God and to those who do not obey the gospel of our Lord Jesus. These will pay the penalty of eternal destruction, away from the presence of the Lord and from the glory of His power” (1:8-9).

•    In chapters 2-3, speaking of the return of Jesus Christ, Paul was sure to include the signs and setting that “the man of lawlessness” (the antichrist) had to arrive. For that to occur the “restrainer” (Holy Spirit) must be removed from restraining him. The Holy Spirit indwells all believers and when He is removed, all believers will be “caught up” in the clouds with the Lord Jesus (1 Thessalonians 4:17). Paul pushes them to pray and serve until this all transpires. “May the Lord direct your hearts into the love of God and into the steadfastness of Christ” (3:5).
    Outline
  2. 1. Comfort During Persecution  ( 1:1⁠–⁠12 )
  3. a. Greetings to the Thessalonians  ( 1:1⁠–⁠4 )
  4. b. Worthy of the Kingdom of God  ( 1:5⁠–⁠12 )
  5. 2. The Day of the Lord  ( 2:1⁠–⁠17 )
  6. a. The Man of Lawlessness  ( 2:1⁠–⁠12 )
  7. b. Stand Firm  ( 2:13⁠–⁠17 )
  8. 3. Concern for the Church  ( 3:1⁠–⁠18 )
  9. a. Request for Prayer  ( 3:1⁠–⁠5 )
  10. b. A Warning against Idleness  ( 3:6⁠–⁠15 )
  11. c. Signature and Final Greetings  ( 3:16⁠–⁠18 )

3 We are bound to thank God always for you, brothers, as it is meet, because that your faith grows exceedingly, and the charity of every one of you all toward each other abounds;2 Thessalonians 1:3
Stats
Counts: 180 characters, 29 words, 143 letters, 58 vowels, 85 consonants
Translation
Greek: ευχαριστειν οφειλομεν τω θεω παντοτε περι υμων αδελφοι καθως αξιον εστιν οτι υπεραυξανει η πιστις υμων και πλεοναζει η αγαπη ενος εκαστου παντων υμων εις αλληλους

Lit: To thank we ought God always concerning you, brothers, just as fitting it is, because is increasing exceedingly the faith of you, and is abounding the love of one each of all you to one another;

KJV: We are bound to thank God always for you, brethren, as it is meet, because that your faith groweth exceedingly, and the charity of every one of you all toward each other aboundeth;

Stats

Counts: 142 characters, 26 words, 116 letters, 47 vowels, 69 consonants
Translation
Greek: ωστε ημας αυτους εν υμιν καυχασθαι εν ταις εκκλησιαις του θεου υπερ της υπομονης υμων και πιστεως εν πασιν τοις διωγμοις υμων και ταις θλιψεσιν αις ανεχεσθε

Lit: so as for ourselves, us in you to boast, in the churches of God, about the perseverance of you, and faith in all the persecutions of you, and in the tribulations that you are bearing.

KJV: So that we ourselves glory in you in the churches of God for your patience and faith in all your persecutions and tribulations that ye endure:

"glory"

"your patience"

"your persecutions"

12 That the name of our Lord Jesus Christ may be glorified in you, and you in Him, according to the grace of our God and the Lord Jesus Christ.2 Thessalonians 1:12
Stats
Rank: #2808 / 31,102 Verses (by popularity)
Counts: 139 characters, 27 words, 108 letters, 41 vowels, 67 consonants
Translation
Greek: οπως ενδοξασθη το ονομα του κυριου ημων ιησου χριστου εν υμιν και υμεις εν αυτω κατα την χαριν του θεου ημων και κυριου ιησου χριστου

Lit: so that may be glorified the name of the Lord of us Jesus in you, and you in Him, according to the grace of the God of us and the Lord Jesus Christ.

KJV: That the name of our Lord Jesus Christ may be glorified in you, and ye in him, according to the grace of our God and the Lord Jesus Christ.

Counts: 160 characters, 28 words, 124 letters, 48 vowels, 76 consonants
Translation

10 With all deceivableness of unrighteousness in them that perish; because they not received the love of the truth, that they might be saved.2 Thessalonians 2:10
Stats
Counts: 142 characters, 22 words, 116 letters, 43 vowels, 73 consonants
Translation
Greek: και εν παση απατη της αδικιας εν τοις απολλυμενοις ανθ ων την αγαπην της αληθειας ουκ εδεξαντο εις το σωθηναι αυτους

Lit: and in every deceit of wickedness unto those perishing, in return for which the love of the truth not they received, in order for to be saved them.

KJV: And with all deceivableness of unrighteousness in them that perish; because they received not the love of the truth, that they might be saved.

14 If any man not obey our word by this epistle, note that man, and have no company with him, that he may be ashamed.2 Thessalonians 3:14
Stats
Rank: #6980 / 31,102 Verses (by popularity)
Counts: 118 characters, 22 words, 90 letters, 33 vowels, 57 consonants
Translation
Greek: ει δε τις ουχ υπακουει τω λογω ημων δια της επιστολης τουτον σημειουσθε και μη συναναμιγνυσθε αυτω ινα εντραπη

Lit: If then anyone not obey this instruction of us through the letter, of this man take note not to mix with him, so that he may be ashamed.

17 The salutation of Paul with my own hand, which is the token in every epistle: so I write.2 Thessalonians 3:17

Translation
Greek: ο ασπασμος τη εμη χειρι παυλου ο εστιν σημειον εν παση επιστολη ουτως γραφω

Lit: The greeting in my own hand — Paul, which is my sign in every letter. In this manner I write.

KJV: The salutation of Paul with mine own hand, which is the token in every epistle: so I write.
